 garth davies , simon fraser university 

 conclusion : taking causality seriously 

 on the subject of the effects of sifs , the available research is overwhelmingly positive .

alright , look , if a program is aimed at racial discrimination , does that make the program itself racist ?
in the case of affirmative action , those programs were designed to counter a racial bias in college admissions of primarily black students capable of doing the coursework but with lower test scores , generally thought to be the result of inferior k-12 schools underfunded because they are in poor neighborhoods .
remember , most public schools are locally funded , so rich neighborhoods have rich schools , poor neighborhoods have poor schools .
the intent of racism is to keep certain races down .
admissions criteria favor applicants from more affluent areas with better schools .
in states where a third of the people are black , for instance , why is it that only a tenth or twentieth of public university admissions are black students ?
that is a racist result that causes harm to black communities and perpetuates poverty , a situation that 's bad for our nation .
that 's why aa programs are n't racist .

here we go again , another rob carrick article trying to talk down single family home ownership and prices .
you have to live somewhere , and by renting you are still paying those exact same maintenance , financing and other costs to someone else , plus their management fees and profit .
and you are almost guaranteed to get less accommodation for the same amount of money , unless you buy a real dud .
the numbers are obviously fudged , 2.5 % annual increase only ?
when i sold my first home after 25 years the annualized rate of increase was 8 % .
my second home has doubled in 10 years .
there will be times , such as now , where the high prices in some communities are slightly skewed against ownership .
however , the bottom line is if you are planning in staying in one location for an extended period , say 4 - 5 years and up , home ownership is the best option .
land transfer tax , real estate agent fees and other closing costs will not be be recovered in 2 - 3 years of ownership .

any company from any state can enter our alaska market .
however , the insurance company 's financial health , premiums , and policies are subject to approval by the alaska division of insurance .
that 's a fact .
to state the obvious again , premera is a washington based company .
premera is already " selling across state lines " .
how is this not clear ?
the problem is that the alaska individual market is small , has very high medical costs , and has more than it 's share of sick people .
the higher the premiums go , the more healthy people choose to take the high stakes gamble of going without insurance and pay the trivial penalty .
those in the middle of a high cost medical treatment certainly are n't going to drop their insurance , if they can pay their premium somehow .
so premiums go yet higher , and the problem compounds itself .
losing healthy people with premium subsidies from the risk pool is not going to improve our situation .

it might interest you to know that hydroelectric power in alaska was pioneered by large mines .
let 's look at juneau .
the nugget creek hydro plant in the mendenhall valley powered the treadwell mine .
the salmon creek dam was the first horseshoe ( constant arc ) dam in the world ( 1914 ) .
the annex creek plant , built for the perserverance mine was the first lake tap in north america ( 1915 ) and has n't stopped generating in over 100 years .
the treadwell ditch ( from eaglecrest to douglas ) was built for hydro - mechanical was later used for hydroelectric power .
salmon creek dam and annex lake are generating hydroelectric power today and supplements the snettisham and dorothy lake projects that power juneau today .
it is said that juneau had electricity before chicago .
it surely had it first in alaska .
thanks to the mines ......

what we need to realize is that there is a world - wide market for health care in developed countries .
single payer systems in europe and elsewhere are effectively subsidized by the chaotic health insurance market in this country , which allows providers , medical device manufacturers , and drug companies to charge much more here , which in turns allows them to give big discounts to the single - payer systems .
so the hospitals wo n't go broke as implied in this article if the u.s. went single - payer .
medicare reimbursements would rise somewhat without a private insurance market , but not as much as private insurance is now reimbursing .
in turn , single - payer systems in other parts of the world would likely   have to reimburse more .
but the end result would be that it would be a heck of a lot cheaper than what we have now .

bro , you probably know this better than i. pontifical seminaries ( as opposed to pontifical faculties at real colleges ) are safe places where bishops and religious superiors can send their seminarians to get easy pontifical degrees and learn how the system works , without being corrupted by theology , science , or the modern world .
the lateran , alfonsianum , antonianum -- all exist so that members of specific religious orders ( or in the case of the lateranum , dioceses ) can get the degrees they need to seem qualified , without being too challenged in terms of academics or belief system . (
which is not to say that some people do n't manage to do serious work anyway . )

we kind of have a hybrid here .
part of your pension -- canada pension plan -- does follow you .
if you move from one employer to another , you do n't start back at square one .
it 's just that cpp ca n't be your only source of retirement income .
some employers share a common pension plan .
the alberta local authorities pension plan is one example .
if you move from one lapp employer to another lapp employer , your pension follows you .
some pension plans allow you to transfer contributions from one pension plan to another if you change employers , though a person may have to " top up " the new plan to get the same pension income at retirement .
this arrangement exists for the federal public service pension plan and several of its provincial counterparts .

hi diii .
sorry for the late response here , but just wanted to explain how the commenting platform works .
civil comments is a crowd - sourced moderation system .
if a comment is deleted , it is not because a moderator at seattle weekly disagrees with it , but because the community of commenters has decided that it is not civil or valuable .
it is not a perfect system , which is why we still have moderators checking in to make sure that the comments that are deleted are deleted for the right reasons ( hate speech , threats , blatant misinformation ) , and not purely for ideological reasons .
we often approve comments that the community disapproves , but rarely do we disapprove comments that the community approves .
here is a video that explains how the platform works .
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mjdjpbazpp8 

 thanks for reading , and i hope you will continue to comment .
mark baumgarten 
 editor in chief

to address your question , i do n't think hillary is an honest person , and i would say that obama is largely honest , although things do n't always turn out how he intends , which could certainly come across as dishonest .
to the greater point about bernie , and socialism in general , is that it 's complicated .
socialism is n't a universal failure .
there are european countries where it has worked , and there are asian countries ( such as china ) where it has , largely , worked .
the answer is n't a blanket statement of " does socialism work or not , " but rather one about what is the proper role of government .
unfettered capitalism has largely proven to be ineffective in a number of areas , so we as a society have decided to regulate it .
i 'm about as much of a capitalist as you 'll find , but i think we can all point out shortcomings with the current system .
moving the top tax rate from 40 % to 50 % is n't the same thing as being " socialist " and we are being intellectually dishonest when we portray it as such .
or ... it would drive the last of the middle income earners out of houses and out of the community , and leave the sf detached model as the preserve of the wealthy .
which is already happening in many areas of metro vancouver .
a better solution would   be to restrict the commodification of housing , and take steps to reduce it .
( in my city of richmond , 47 % of the housing units in the city centre are sold and empty ! ) .
we could restrict the purchase of residential housing by non residents and non citizens , we could tie capital gains exemptions into income tax paid and the   length of time you have live in your house .
we could increase taxation on speculation and flipping .
increasing tax on   those who want to stay in the homes they have raised their families in , in the neighbourhoods they have volunteered and contributed to , should be the last resort .
